  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ce8cdff6-0e49-4517-91bf-5bad04d2c8f5'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer9098331412254367311"><i>If you could read my mind, you wouldn't be smiling.</i><br/><br/> Samantha McAllister looks just like the rest of the popular girls in her junior class.   <span id="freeText9098331412254367311" style="display:none"><i>If you could read my mind, you wouldn't be smiling.</i><br /><br /> Samantha McAllister looks just like the rest of the popular girls in her junior class. But hidden beneath the straightened hair and expertly applied makeup is a secret that her friends would never understand: Sam has Purely-Obsessional OCD and is consumed by a stream of dark thoughts and worries that she can't turn off. <br /><br />Second-guessing every move, thought, and word makes daily life a struggle, and it doesn't help that her lifelong friends will turn toxic at the first sign of a wrong outfit, wrong lunch, or wrong crush. Yet Sam knows she'd be <i>truly</i> crazy to leave the protection of the most popular girls in school. So when Sam meets Caroline, she has to keep her new friend with a refreshing sense of humor and no style a secret, right up there with Sam's weekly visits to her psychiatrist.<br /><br />Caroline introduces Sam to Poet's Corner, a hidden room and a tight-knit group of misfits who have been ignored by the school at large. Sam is drawn to them immediately, especially a guitar-playing guy with a talent for verse, and starts to discover a whole new side of herself. Slowly, she begins to feel more "normal" than she ever has as part of the popular crowd . . . until she finds a new reason to question her sanity and all she holds dear.</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/609003-is-the-portrayal-of-ocd-accurate-in-this">Is the portrayal of OCD accurate in this novel?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_609003'><a id="like_count_community_question_609003" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/609003?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">11 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F23341894-every-last-word">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/609003-is-the-portrayal-of-ocd-accurate-in-this">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/609003-is-the-portrayal-of-ocd-accurate-in-this">See all 6 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/104203853-shuichi-saihara"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/104203853-shuichi-saihara">Shuichi Saihara</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I have OCD, and reading this book made me feel incredibly belittled. Love doesn't cure everything, and that's what this book is saying. Sure, you may <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I have OCD, and reading this book made me feel incredibly belittled. Love doesn't cure everything, and that's what this book is saying. Sure, you may find someone who makes you feel good, but having a romantic relationship doesn't solve all of your problems. A serious disorder cannot be solved by romance, that just isn't how things work. So I dont think it portrays OCD at all, if anything it just romanticizes it, which is heartbreaking.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1310570787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17974040751267030209"><b>This book is a saccharine sweet fairy tale version of a very real mental illness, Obsessive-Compulsive Disorder (OCD), as well as the very serious issue of bullying, without true emotional depth</b>. It's the equivalent of ordering a black coffee at Starbucks, taking a sip, only to find out that you've been given a caramel mocha instead. It is unrealistic, it is a Disney-fied version of real life, complete with a happy ending.<br/><br/>Real life doesn't work that way. Mental illnesses don't work that way. I k</span>
  <span id="freeText17974040751267030209" style="display:none"><b>This book is a saccharine sweet fairy tale version of a very real mental illness, Obsessive-Compulsive Disorder (OCD), as well as the very serious issue of bullying, without true emotional depth</b>. It's the equivalent of ordering a black coffee at Starbucks, taking a sip, only to find out that you've been given a caramel mocha instead. It is unrealistic, it is a Disney-fied version of real life, complete with a happy ending.<br /><br />Real life doesn't work that way. Mental illnesses don't work that way. I know very well it doesn't work that way because I've got it.<br /><br /><b>I have OCPD</b> (obsessive-compulsive personality disorder). It's a lesser form of OCD. I don't obsessively count things, I don't get massive panic attacks, I don't get major anxiety attacks, but I know what it feels like to have your own mind turn on you at times. My mind is constantly racing at hyperspeed. I can't relax. It takes me 2 hours to fall asleep every night because I can't be at rest. Like the main character in this book, I have survived on very little sleep for a very, very long time. I'm constantly tired.<br /><br />When something falls out of pattern in my day. When I don't get a certain machine at the gym. When I can't do this or that at a certain time. I do not get major panic attacks over them, but at the same time, things just feel wrong. Certain things, minor to others, will ruin my day. "Why can't you just use another machine?" It doesn't work like that.<br /><br />Most often, if people ask, I just laugh it off, because honestly, I don't care. I feel like my OCD does make me a better person, in some ways. I know I work more efficiently than most, I know that my boss loves that part of my mind because it ensures I'm THE BEST EMPLOYEE EVER because I will not let anything slip through the cracks. I know that this part of my personality drives me towards knowledge because that, too, is an obsession. I'm not ashamed, but I still know how the character in this book feels, knowing you're not entirely normal, and hiding it from most people you know so that you won't be judged, because most people can and will judge anyone with a mental disorder.<br /><br />I know I'm not my mental illness. I think I'm an awesome person. I'm smart, I'm funny, I'm pretty good looking for my age. But at the same time, there's a part of me that just constantly whispers <b>"You're not normal. You'll never be normal."</b> It takes a lot of effort go to through my day sometimes.<br /><br />I know what OCD is, <b>and for me, this book does not accurately portray it.</b> As I mentioned before, this is a book published by Disney, and it is more for the dreamy <i>Perks of a Wallflower</i> crowd than anyone who truly wants to understand the depths behind this mental illness. This book is <b>far too sweet, far too improbably, far too unrealistic.</b><br /><br />The main character, Samantha, has OCD. She is a repetitive thinker. This feeling of obsession does not persist throughout the book, <b>her mental illness only resurfaces occasionally. There is no feeling that she is constantly under the weight of this mental illness the way a real mental illness should be.</b><blockquote>
  <i>When I finally pulled into the driveway that evening, the last digit was resting on a six, so I backed out again and drove around the block a few times until the odometer stopped where it belonged. And now I have to do that every time I park.</i>
</blockquote>Everything in life is perfect, pretty much, understanding mom, fantastic psychiatrist (not all psychiatrists are that awesome, I assure you), and <b>she is a part of the popular "Mean Girls" at school.</b> She hates them, but she fits in perfectly well with them, and <b>she is perfectly able to disguise her OCD despite having been diagnosed with a severe form of it by the age of 10.</b> I assure you, this is not true in real life. Nobody who has OCD can conceal it that well, particularly not a child. It is almost impossible that Samantha can fit in and disguise herself as normal to the most conceited, most judgmental, most observant group of girls on campus, girls who have known her since childhood.<br /><br /><b>And then there's the artificially sweet and improbable artsy-fartsy little Poetry Corner with whom she falls in</b> when she tries to make some true friends, people who understand her, people who express their emotions through words and poetry and song. A private little club that nobody knows about. Gag me, really. Real life doesn't have this shit.<blockquote>
  <i>As I scan the room, taking in the slips of paper scattered around me, I think I catch Caroline and pixie-cut girl look at each other. “What is this place?” I ask again, hearing the amazement in my own voice.<br />Pixie Cut answers me. “We call it Poet’s Corner.”</i>
</blockquote>Real life doesn't have friends with whom you can constantly click, with whom you immediately reveal your inner self.<br /><br /><b>This book not only deals with OCD, but with the issue of bullying, and it deals with it in a manner that feels completely false.</b> The main character may not be a bully herself, but she does so out of peer pressure. Her group, the Mean Girls, have constantly taunted and made fun of others whom they deem inferior.<blockquote>
  <i>“A-A-A-Andrew…” to the tune of the Chia Pet jingle, and then she starts cracking up.<br /><br />“How can you not remember Andrew? That kid stuttered so badly he couldn’t even say his name. We used to follow him around singing that song.…You have to remember this!”<br /><br />Oh, God. I do. It’s all starting to come back to me, and when she sings that horrible song again, I can see Kaitlyn and me in our skirts and ponytails, trailing behind him on the playground while he covered his ears, tears streaming down his face, trying to run away from us. We never let him get far.</i>
</blockquote>Bullying is a very, very serious issue, and this book <b>does not give weight to it.</b> It glosses over the fact that the character was a bully. It <b>never truly delves into the mental process and the depths behind such an act</b>. The main character feels bad about it, she feels a lot of remorse, but there is never any feeling of true emotion or sincerity upon her reflection into it. <br /><br />There have been a lot of bullying stories in the news. There's so much that goes on in the mind of a person who tortures someone so much. <b>This book should have portrayed the feeling of self-hate, of insecurity, of the darkness in the mind of the person who does the bullying. In my opinion, this book completely failed at it.</b><br /><br />Again, this is a Disney-fied book about mental illnesses and bullying. I understand that the author does not have OCD, and she is doing her best to portray a mental illness. One does not have to have a mental disease to write about it, but<b> a book about such serious issues should feel realistic and relatable to the reader, and particularly, one who suffers from it</b>. This book failed to do that, for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17974040751267030209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1758323924" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14865781409717840104"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br/><br/>Great. Thank you, book. Knowing what I now know, I’ll have to read you all over again. Bet you’re real happy right now, aren’t ya?<br/><br/>Mind-blowing, unexpected turn of events.<br/><br/>I fell head over heels for this EVERY LAST WORD heart-warming creature. <br/><br/>It’s a lyrical, theme-filled and romantic story about OCD-sufferer Samantha McAllister. She’s obsessed about the number 3, among other things. But no one can know about that, especially not her popular bitchy friends, the Eights.<br/><br/>With the help of Ca</span>
  <span id="freeText14865781409717840104" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br /><br />Great. Thank you, book. Knowing what I now know, I’ll have to read you all over again. Bet you’re real happy right now, aren’t ya?<br /><br />Mind-blowing, unexpected turn of events.<br /><br />I fell head over heels for this EVERY LAST WORD heart-warming creature. <br /><br />It’s a lyrical, theme-filled and romantic story about OCD-sufferer Samantha McAllister. She’s obsessed about the number 3, among other things. But no one can know about that, especially not her popular bitchy friends, the Eights.<br /><br />With the help of Caroline, Sam discovers a secret poets club. Her first chapter to becoming a braver, more assertive and accepting person starts right there. And who knows, maybe it’ll even bring her love?<br /><br />Despite the stereotyped Eights who bring a contained amount of shallowness and ‘‘clichédness’’ to the story, it’s a deep, meaningful book. And hey, even the Eights situation has a realistic quality. <br /><br />Many of us understand what it feels like to have to end a relationship that’s been going for a long time, because of the natural phenomena that are called ‘‘growing up’’ and ‘‘finding our true self.’’ YET, it never is easy.<br /><br />I loved the flirting. It didn’t last long, but god did it captivate me. I was so close to the paper I thought I might, by some magical luck, step into the book to join the flirty conversation. Because why not? The more, the merrier. <br /><br />Beautiful, beautiful book. Seriously recommend. You don’t even have to be a fan of mental illness books to love this. You really don’t and that’s the beauty of it. It can appeal to a large group of people. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>

<div id="review_1201994684" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1201994684" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1201994684?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1201994684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2059526303778750957"><b>FINALLY! A mental health book with excellent rep.</b> I'm so...I'm so freaking emotional right now?! This was incredible and you could feel the realism, the love, and the respect on every page. It also totally highlights how having a mental illness <i>can</i> be devastating, but noooo it doesn't have to ruin your life. Your brain being different isn't crazy or broken or wrong and I just...<br/><br/>thankkkkk you to this book for existing. I feel like I've read so many crappy reps of mental illness lately it's just <i>e</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2059526303778750957" style="display:none"><b>FINALLY! A mental health book with excellent rep.</b> I'm so...I'm so freaking emotional right now?! This was incredible and you could feel the realism, the love, and the respect on every page. It also totally highlights how having a mental illness <i>can</i> be devastating, but noooo it doesn't have to ruin your life. Your brain being different isn't crazy or broken or wrong and I just...<br /><br />thankkkkk you to this book for existing. I feel like I've read so many crappy reps of mental illness lately it's just <i>encouraging</i> to finally read one that <br />a) cares about mentally ill teens<br />b) actually has POSITIVE REP of medication and therapy<br />c) has lovely and supportive parents<br />d) doesn't use romance as a cure<br />e) shows dark sides but also ways to build yourself back up<br />f) SAYS YOU CAN STILL BE MENTALLY ILL AND HAVE A GOOD LIFE<br /><br /><b>Also one thing I REALLY liked about the therapy too is that: it was professionally done.</b> Like usually with books it's two teens doing their version of "therapy" (like exposure therapy is a huge one &gt;_&gt;) and it's always so problematic (imo) because therapy needs to be done with a professional. Sure you can do things for yourself and with the support of family/friends, but I hate hate hate the trope of two potential love-interest teens doing therapy together and falling in love. THIS DIDN'T HAVE THAT AND I AM GLAD.<br /><br /><b>Also so Sam is sort of part of the "in crowd" at school, and she knows they're pretty poisonous but she doesn't want to leave.</b> When I saw this in the blurb it was like cue !! eyeroll !! I'm so tired !! right now!! <b>But it was reallllly well done.</b> Like Sam's Queen B friends were, yes, really nasty at times, but they were also PEOPLE. So they were kind and sometimes funny and just??? They were real people, so not cliche at all! (But ultimately: still poisonous haha.) I also really relate to Sam <i>not</i> wanting to leave because sometimes having friends who passive aggressively wound you is still better than nothing. (HEART BREAKS...but I just like how Sam ended up dealing with this aspect.)<br /><br /><b>OK and Sam?! Best narrator.</b> She was interesting and scared and complex and just ahhh!!! HHH!HHH The kind of narrator I love to read about honestly. &lt;3 Her OCD is also more about thought-spirals (so more like in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35504431.Turtles_All_the_Way_Down" title="Turtles All the Way Down by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Turtles All the Way Down</a>) and I'm sooo glad it was repped like this because it was done so well.<br /><br />(Also author's note says she consulted with multiple doctors about her rep AND she based it off a 14 year old girl who had input as well! CAN I JUUUUUST SAY THIS IS HOW YOU SHOULD DO MENTAL HEALTH IN BOOKS.)<br /><br />(And also the only reason it's not 5 full stars is just because while I totally adored it, it didn't QUIT hit me as deeply as some of my other total favourite books have. So this is nothing against the book!! Just me still hungover from The Cruel Prince. It's like a 4.5-stars!!)<br /><br /><b>And AJ + Sam = the cutest.</b> It was seriously sooo stinkin' cute. And AJ was an anxious guitar-playing cinnamon scone as well, so basically what is not to love here. I also liked how their relationship was healthy. Imagine that. HEALTHY ROMANCe. Omg this book is just hitting me in all the feels.<br /><br />I shall go sit in a bucket of cornflakes now. I'm in so much appreciation wow.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2059526303778750957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4078859782083322187">this book is sooo me. i loved it when i first read it a few years ago, and i love it even more now. down to every last word.<br/><br/>as someone with a psychology background, i have to praise TIS for her very real portrayal of OCD. i cant even begin to tell you how often people are misinformed about the disorder or how debilitating common misconceptions of OCD can be. i really admire how the story was inspired by someone close to TIS who has the disorder, because it makes its representation so personal an</span>
  <span id="freeText4078859782083322187" style="display:none">this book is sooo me. i loved it when i first read it a few years ago, and i love it even more now. down to every last word.<br /><br />as someone with a psychology background, i have to praise TIS for her very real portrayal of OCD. i cant even begin to tell you how often people are misinformed about the disorder or how debilitating common misconceptions of OCD can be. i really admire how the story was inspired by someone close to TIS who has the disorder, because it makes its representation so personal and the storytelling/writing definitely shows it. <br /><br />im also so enamoured by how this story is a love letter to words. from their healing powers to inspirational strength, words play such a large role in this story and sams management of her OCD. i think many readers, myself included, understand sams connection with words (whether its poetry or song lyrics or anything else) and can see themselves in that aspect of the story. <br /><br />this is such a touching, motivational, and highly informational read. definitely a recommendable favourite!!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>5 stars</i></b></span>

  <span id="freeText2980696991433397839" style="display:none">*I received this book from the publisher in exchange for an honest review*<br /><br />What a beautiful book. . Definitely one of the best contemporary books I've read this year. Sam's story was so moving and my heart was honestly pounding towards the end. This book touches on some really serious topics like depression, anxiety, and mental disorders, but I thought that Tamara Ireland Stone did it beautifully. One of my favorite parts (which was a huge part) was the poetry in this book. This is the type of book that makes YOU want to write.. And it doesn't even have to be good. Just to express yourself and to try.. I feel like many people that have been through high school will relate to what Sam goes through.. The pressures from your peers, and sadly, your "friends". I loved Sam's character and was so, so pleased by her progress just like Sue throughout the story. This book made me laugh, cry, and really inspired me to write more. Thank you Tamara for this beautiful book!</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781484706275" href="/book/show/28044076-every-last-word">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Warda by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/45365270-nadhira-satria">Nadhira Satria</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=i-fell-in-love">i-fell-in-love</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16733055708091187538">Books on mental health hit me in a way no other story does. It’s personal and intimate and I’m seen and understood in a way I want to be seen and understood. <br/>It’s even better when these stories include therapy sessions and showcase the positive impact they can have. A good therapist can do that. <br/><br/>It’s made me want to read more books on mental health and become more of an advocate for it. <br/><br/>This particular story deals with OCD alongside anxiety. I didn’t know much about this book going into it and I</span>
  <span id="freeText16733055708091187538" style="display:none">Books on mental health hit me in a way no other story does. It’s personal and intimate and I’m seen and understood in a way I want to be seen and understood. <br />It’s even better when these stories include therapy sessions and showcase the positive impact they can have. A good therapist can do that. <br /><br />It’s made me want to read more books on mental health and become more of an advocate for it. <br /><br />This particular story deals with OCD alongside anxiety. I didn’t know much about this book going into it and I preferred it that way. Our main character goes on a journey of combatting her mental health and I particularly enjoy that just because I’m able to see how it helps the main character and what parallels I can draw from their lives into mine. <br /><br />Highly recommend it if you’re into contemporaries, want to find out more on mental health and what it means to have good people and safe space around you. <br /><br />Picking up all the books written by Tamara Ireland Stone. <br /><br /><br />——————————<br /><br />Have been meaning to get to this for the longest of times. And now thanks to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/nadhirasatria" rel="nofollow noopener">Nadhira</a> I am!</span>

<div id="review_1106772077" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1106772077" />
    <a title="April (Aprilius Maximus)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus"><img alt="April (Aprilius Maximus)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589331862p2/20658145.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1106772077?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="April (Aprilius Maximus)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="April (Aprilius Maximus)" href="/user/show/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus">April (Aprilius Maximus)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus?shelf=anxiety">anxiety</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1106772077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12958969249430385389">Special thanks to NetGalley and Disney Hyperion for this review copy! <br/>This book was phenomenal. It was one of the best young adult contemporaries that I've read that deals with mental illness. The main character, Sam, has OCD which is an anxiety disorder. I suffer from an anxiety disorder too, so I really wanted to read this and see how I could connect with it and how well Tamara Ireland Stone portrayed it. I have to say, she did this fantastically. You really get a feel for what it's like to go</span>
  <span id="freeText12958969249430385389" style="display:none">Special thanks to NetGalley and Disney Hyperion for this review copy! <br />This book was phenomenal. It was one of the best young adult contemporaries that I've read that deals with mental illness. The main character, Sam, has OCD which is an anxiety disorder. I suffer from an anxiety disorder too, so I really wanted to read this and see how I could connect with it and how well Tamara Ireland Stone portrayed it. I have to say, she did this fantastically. You really get a feel for what it's like to go through her mental disorder and I think people who don't suffer from mental illness firsthand will really get to see what it's like and the effects that it can have on a person, their life and the people around them. <br />I was honestly hooked from the start. It had a plot-line that kept me completely engaged the entire time and the romance was portrayed so realistically and was so swoon-worthy it had me smiling to myself while I was reading. I just think that the romance is so real and fun to read about and it was perfectly paced. The characters were all great! I loved her psychologist and the poetry group and everyone in it so much! I just felt for them all and felt like I was friends with them too by the end! I also loved how poetry was incorporated into the novel. It was done wonderfully and the poems were all so unique and different and lovely. <br />The only criticism I have for this book is that there is a HUGE absence of Sam's family. They appear a couple of times, but other than that, I don't know anything about them at all! I really wanted them to be fleshed out a lot more because I feel as though they played a huge role in helping Sam through everything (especially at the start and end of the novel, as well as before the events in the novel even happen.) <br />Other than that, what a beautiful, engaging and inspiring novel. Absolutely adored it! </span>
  <a data-text-id="12958969249430385389" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <a title="Beverly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13095060-beverly"><img alt="Beverly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466964369p2/13095060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1555231776" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13986457209924278328">O.M.G. this book, I loved it, like legit loved it. It starts out odd, but I think that’s just because I wasn’t really sure what I was getting into, but once I got into it I fell in love!<br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Everyone’s got something. Some people are just better actors than others.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>Samantha McAlister is one of the most popular girls in school, from the outside looking in her life is perfect. She is pretty, intelligent, and friends with the right people. No one knows she suffers from OCD, which is real a </span>
  <span id="freeText13986457209924278328" style="display:none">O.M.G. this book, I loved it, like legit loved it. It starts out odd, but I think that’s just because I wasn’t really sure what I was getting into, but once I got into it I fell in love!<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Everyone’s got something. Some people are just better actors than others.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Samantha McAlister is one of the most popular girls in school, from the outside looking in her life is perfect. She is pretty, intelligent, and friends with the right people. No one knows she suffers from OCD, which is real a testament to how little she trusts her friends. <br><br>It’s the beginning of the school year and Samantha meets a new friend who changes her life and opens up a whole new world for her. She joins a secret group, Poetry Corner. Writing allows her to express herself and her new friends help her realize what’s important. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456448473i/18235973._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved this book, I mean epically loved it. I related so much to Samantha and you don’t have to be OCD to understand her. I think that just about everyone can relate to how Sam felt. Most everyone struggles with belonging and fear of judgment at some point in their lives. I love the lessons Sam learned and how she grew throughout the story. <br><br>I know I am not everyone’s cuppa tea and I am seriously okay with that, but it took me years to be okay with that. I wish I had realized it sooner. I love that <i>Every Last Word</i> helps teach that message. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Sam: Do you always say exactly what you're thinking?<br><br>AJ: I try to. I like to know where I stand with people, and I figure I owe them the same courtesy. I mean, I'm never rude or hurtful about it, but I don't see any reason to be fake. That's a lot of work” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Be kind, be honest and be you and move on. It’s a great message and I adored reading this story! Highly recommend it for everyone!!<br><br>I listened to this audiobook and loved the narration! <br><br><i>Teasers created by me with stock images purchased from depositphotos.</i><br><br>

<div id="review_1223711509" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1223711509" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1223711509?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24795570-every-last-word">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=my-favorite-covers">my-favorite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=arc-netgalley">arc-netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1223711509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13056753743157220369"><b>FINALLLYYYYY on sale!!! Go buy it!!! NOOOW!</b> Click <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Every-Last-Word-Not-part-ebook/dp/B00RY6YX56/ref=sr_1_1_twi_1_kin?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1434458673&sr=1-1&keywords=every+last+word' rel='nofollow noopener'>HERE</a> to purchase<br/><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>If you could read my mind, you wouldn't be smiling.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Sometimes a book just calls to you. Sometimes it consumes your every waking thought until you can finally pick it up. Sometimes.....when you get an opportunity to read a book before anyone else you realize just how lucky you are, because you just <i>knew</i> from the moment you saw it that it was going to be special, perfect, just what you've been dying to read. That's exactly how I </span>
  <span id="freeText13056753743157220369" style="display:none"><b>FINALLLYYYYY on sale!!! Go buy it!!! NOOOW!</b> Click <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Every-Last-Word-Not-part-ebook/dp/B00RY6YX56/ref=sr_1_1_twi_1_kin?s=books&amp;ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1434458673&amp;sr=1-1&amp;keywords=every+last+word" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a> to purchase<br><br><br><br><b>
  <i>If you could read my mind, you wouldn't be smiling.</i>
</b><br><br>Sometimes a book just calls to you. Sometimes it consumes your every waking thought until you can finally pick it up. Sometimes.....when you get an opportunity to read a book before anyone else you realize just how lucky you are, because you just <i>knew</i> from the moment you saw it that it was going to be special, perfect, just what you've been dying to read. That's exactly how I felt about this book-<b>From the moment I saw this book, I knew I had to have it.</b> There was just something about the blurb that spoke to me on a visceral level, and I knew that if I got it from the publisher, I'd love it. Not often do I like my ARCs...but <b>from the moment I opened this book, it owned my soul.</b><br><br>This is a story about a girl with OCD. A girl who, for all intents and purposes, hasn't told anyone about her condition. The dark thoughts that plague her mind daily make it difficult to function in every day activities that others take for granted. She struggles to maintain the facade of being a 'normal' girl around her popular friends who expect only the best from her, and she can't find peace at night, so she has to take sleeping medications. Her nature is to latch onto something and grip it tight, to search and investigate until all outlets are exhausted and she has enough information to satisfy her hunger for any information concerning what she became obsessed with in the first place.<br><br>Then one day she meets a new friend, Caroline, and what she shows her will change her life. But at the head of Poet's Corner (The place Caroline showed her) is a boy who doesn't like her much, but she can't seem to figure out why. She's told she isn't allowed to join the secret club, that she isn't welcome. But Samantha knows in her heart that this club is just what she needs-she knows that it's just the outlet her OCD and inner turmoils need and that it could possibly change the way she thinks every day-it might be the thing that helps her focus her thoughts and dilute the obsession she feels at every waking moment. So, she sets out to prove herself not only to the group, but to the boy who has shunned her without a backward glance. <b>Why does he look at her like he can't stand to be near her...and why does it bother her so much?</b><br><br>This book touched me so deeply. It isn't simply that Samantha has OCD and struggles internally, it's <i>how</i> she struggles. It's the way it crushes her spirit again and again, yet she continues to fight and claw and strive to be the person she wants to be. She broke down so many times, yet she let no one see how broken she was. <b>I loved that.</b> I loved how strong her character was and how she never pitied herself...well, not a ton, anyway.<br><br>But what I loved most?? I'll just come out and say it: AJ. <b>I loved loved <i>loved</i> AJ.</b> He was sweet, kind, thoughtful, and he induced so many butterflies that I was choking on them. I think there's something to be said for a subtle, YA romance. Every look, every touch, every <i>moment</i> means something...it's not fleeting and the romance doesn't rely on sex or physical contact. <b>We get to build a deep, meaningful relationship</b> through words and crucial experiences. And when they finally <i>do</i> touch, kiss, or get physical?? <b>It's explosive.</b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/giphy%2024_zpsbslfendz.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428329344ra/14406631.gif" alt=" photo giphy 24_zpsbslfendz.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Without being able to use quotes I feel a tad naked, but I think I said everything that needed to be said without them. I loved reading this story so much, and I was so so sad when it started to come to an end. <b>AJ and Samantha were two amazing characters that I became viscerally attached to and I never wanted their story to end.</b> It was beautiful, heartfelt, and I never once felt the writing was forced when it came to her OCD. It was as natural as breathing and the author's words flowed so seamlessly that it became difficult to put the book down and separate myself from this amazing story. I am so appreciative I got this ARC, but I cannot wait to read the final work-I am pre-ordering the hardback as soon as I finish this review. I will definitely be looking at other works from this author and I will be re-reading this story over and over again. <b>Every Last Word.</b><br><br><br><br>*ARC provided by Netgalley in exchange for an honest review*<br><br><br><b>**I will be adding quotes once the book is released**</b><br><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/%20" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="60" width="139" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409285880i/10960212.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><br><br><br>*****************************************************************<br><br><b>MY FIRST NETGALLEY APPROVAL FROM DISNEY!!! <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_n6wmjhdpa71trd5j4o3_250_zps4nxrsd9v.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427899135ra/14332122.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_n6wmjhdpa71trd5j4o3_250_zps4nxrsd9v.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>And wouldn't ya know it, I really wanted this one XD</b></span>

<div id="review_1528402485" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1528402485" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1528402485?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2016-audios">2016-audios</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2016-ya-challenge">2016-ya-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1528402485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11239794644039917014"><b>4 stars!</b> <br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%208/023cd4b8-a0aa-40c8-badd-495d15cfbd95_zpstds94l30.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455754751i/18146724._SX540_.jpg' alt=' photo 023cd4b8-a0aa-40c8-badd-495d15cfbd95_zpstds94l30.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>4 stars for my 4th YA book of the year! <br/><br/><i>Every Last Word</i> is a story about a teenage girl who is dealing with OCD. Samantha McAllister appears to be perfect on the outside, but inside she's a mess. She constantly worries about her friends finding out about her condition and the fact that she sees a psychiatrist. When Sam meets Caroline and gets introduced to the kids in Poet's Corner, everything changes for her. She finds herself coming out of her shell and embracing who she is. <br/><br/>Saman</span>
  <span id="freeText11239794644039917014" style="display:none"><b>4 stars!</b> <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%208/023cd4b8-a0aa-40c8-badd-495d15cfbd95_zpstds94l30.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455754751i/18146724._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo 023cd4b8-a0aa-40c8-badd-495d15cfbd95_zpstds94l30.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>4 stars for my 4th YA book of the year! <br><br><i>Every Last Word</i> is a story about a teenage girl who is dealing with OCD. Samantha McAllister appears to be perfect on the outside, but inside she's a mess. She constantly worries about her friends finding out about her condition and the fact that she sees a psychiatrist. When Sam meets Caroline and gets introduced to the kids in Poet's Corner, everything changes for her. She finds herself coming out of her shell and embracing who she is. <br><br>Samantha was a likable character. I felt for her. I love how she dealt with all of her struggles and overcame her issues. Sam learns not only to accept herself but to stand up for herself and have friends that accept who she is. She was strong on her own, but I love her relationship with AJ as well. AJ really deep down cares for Sam and is there for her no matter what he finds out about her. They were a great couple. <br><br>One other thing I enjoyed about this book is that there was a twist I didn't see coming. I love when that happens! I found this story to be moving and beautiful. I love the poetry and the writing style. I listened to the audio version and the narration was average- not great or bad. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11239794644039917014" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1565893543?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=ya-contemporary-romance">ya-contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=hardcover">hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1565893543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18351780880841177760"><b> 4 stars! </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “If you could read my mind, you wouldn't be smiling.” </i> </b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450539544ra/17441330.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Every Last Word is the story of Sam, a teenage girl with a debilitating case of OCD. Not the kind like you and I think, where it's like people keeping things nice and neat, but one that messes with her sense of reality. One of the popular girls at school, she is forever in fear of her group of friends finding out her secret and ridiculing her for it.<br/><br/>One day she discovers a new group of people at school she never really noticed be</span>
  <span id="freeText18351780880841177760" style="display:none"><b> 4 stars! </b><br><br><b> <i> “If you could read my mind, you wouldn't be smiling.” </i> </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450539544ra/17441330.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Every Last Word is the story of Sam, a teenage girl with a debilitating case of OCD. Not the kind like you and I think, where it's like people keeping things nice and neat, but one that messes with her sense of reality. One of the popular girls at school, she is forever in fear of her group of friends finding out her secret and ridiculing her for it.<br><br>One day she discovers a new group of people at school she never really noticed before. With some encouragement from a new friend, Sam makes an effort to join this new group who loves poetry and expression. But her past and her friends make it difficult for this new group of people to trust her, and she must prove her worth to them.<br><br><b> <i> “I didn’t go there looking for you. I went looking for me.” My voice is soft, low, and shaky. “But now, here you are, and somehow, in finding you, I think I’ve found myself.” </i> </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381677350ra/5178702.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I liked this book a lot more than I thought I would. This is an author I've always been meaning to read, she has another series that looks good but I never got around to it. I love reading stories where the main character becomes disillusioned with their current life style and looks to other ways of spending their time. It's one of the better ways of promoting character development in a story (and we all know I must have my character development!) so I really enjoyed this book.<br><br>I liked the romance aspect because I wasn't really expecting it. AJ was a little bit too good to be true and I thought he forgave Sam for her past a little bit too quickly, but ultimately it worked for the book as a whole.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450147590ra/17385411.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I did guess the "surprise" fairly early on, but I loved that part of the story. It's amazing what the human mind can do and a great added twist to the plot. I also liked the use of words and how they helped Sam get through rough spots. Her OCD was based on words and thoughts, and by joining the poetry group she learned a way to manage and control them in a healthy way.<br><br><b> <i> “Mistakes. Trial and error. Same thing. Mistakes are how we learned to walk and run and that hot things burn when you touch them. You’ve made mistakes all your life and you’re going to keep making them.” </i> </b><br><br>I will say, if I tried to write poetry, this would be me:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456946647i/18299684.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="18351780880841177760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <i>“My friends can’t know about my OCD or the debilitating, uncontrollable thoughts, because my friends are normal. And perfect. They pride themselves on normalcy and perfection, and they can’t ever find out how far I am from those two things.”</i>

</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433326807i/15083430.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was a YA story about a girl with OCD.<br><br>I felt quite sorry for Sam in this story, her friends obviously made her feel quite awkward at times, and it wasn’t nice how they refused to even call her ‘Sam’ instead of ‘Samantha’. It was bad enough that she had to deal with the OCD, without having to constantly worry what her friends would think if they found out about it.<br><br><b>
  <i>“When I finally pulled into the driveway that evening, the last digit was resting on a six, so I backed out again and drove around the block a few times until the odometer stopped where it belonged. And now I have to do that every time I park.”</i>

It was nice that she was finally able to be herself a bit more, and had friends that she felt she could rely on.<br><br><b>

<div id="review_1240430435" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1240430435" />
    <a title="✦❋Arianna✦❋" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23370948-arianna"><img alt="✦❋Arianna✦❋" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420671997p2/23370948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1240430435?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✦❋Arianna✦❋" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✦❋Arianna✦❋" href="/user/show/23370948-arianna">✦❋Arianna✦❋</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1240430435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8020535479153280258"><b>3.5 Stars!!</b><br/><br/>I don’t know what I expected reading this book, but I expected something a little different. It wasn’t the best book I’ve read with this premise, but it wasn’t the worst either. Honestly I expected something more emotional and/or more moving. Needless to say the author failed (a little) to keep me truly invested in the story. It was a good story, like my rating says, but it could have been much better if it would have been longer. <br/><br/><i>“Every Last Word”</i> is the story of Samantha ‘Sam’, a gi</span>
  <span id="freeText8020535479153280258" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars!!</b><br /><br />I don’t know what I expected reading this book, but I expected something a little different. It wasn’t the best book I’ve read with this premise, but it wasn’t the worst either. Honestly I expected something more emotional and/or more moving. Needless to say the author failed (a little) to keep me truly invested in the story. It was a good story, like my rating says, but it could have been much better if it would have been longer. <br /><br /><i>“Every Last Word”</i> is the story of Samantha ‘Sam’, a girl who’s a junior in high school. While she looks and apparently acts like all the other popular girls in her junior class, Samantha is nothing like them. She’s ‘different’, she knows it and all her life tried to hide it, to hide‘the truth’ about herself. Samantha has Purely-Obsessional OCD and all her life lied by omission to anyone who came across. She can’t turn off her thoughts and she can’t sleep without being drugged into it. She also sees a therapist. Her mind never stops working and what scares her the most is the fact that sometimes her thoughts are dark and disturbing. Samantha wants to belong, to be accepted, to be needed and wanted, she wants to be ‘normal’. She struggles every day to appear ‘normal’ in front of ‘the Eights’, her ‘friends’ and in front of everyone else. <br /><br />Samantha becomes Sam when she meets a girl, Caroline, girl who will change her life forever. She finds out what Poet’s Corner is, she meets a boy who will make her a better human being and she will find who she truly is and what she truly wants to do with her life. <br /><br />I don’t think I’ve read any book about a character with this mental illness –OCD, so I can’t say much about this aspect of the story, if it’s done well or not, compared with other books. But what I can say is that it was done in a respectful way. However, I expected to be more emotional invested since it’s about a mental illness. Maybe because I felt some aspects of the story were a little rushed and also because the story felt too short.<br /> <br />Samantha was a likeable character and I have to say I felt for her and her struggles felt real for the most part. I’m sure some readers will relate with her, even if she suffers from OCD, because let’s face it, many of us, if not all of us want to belong, to be ‘normal’ or ‘perfect’ or to be accepted. Even if she struggles with her mental illness, she is a strong heroine, determined to have a future like a ‘normal’ person, to win a scholarship, to go to college, to have something meaningful with a boy. Her character growth is well done and I liked very much the new Samantha, – Sam. <br /><br />The cast of supporting character are fantastic, engaging and endearing. (I’m talking about Sam’s new friends) I loved Caroline. A lot! She was such a great friend. She’s sweet and funny, supportive, considerate and I loved how good she was for Sam. I loved their interactions and how much Sam learns from her new friend. And AJ...*swoon*. That’s right...he made me swoon. He was amazing. There was a moment when I wondered if he truly is as amazing as he seemed from the beginning. I’m glad he turn out to be what I hoped. He was sweet, considerate and so thoughtful. He was perfect for Sam and he was what she really needed. As for Sam’s friends ‘the Eights'...what can I say?! They were horrible. <br /> <br />There’s a very interesting twist in the story I never see it coming. Wow! Needless to say from that moment I had to know more.<br /><br />An important aspect in this story is bullying. This aspect is not very developed, because this book it’s not about that, but the author reminds us how this kind of behavior can change someone.<br /><br />Overall – an engaging read, with a likeable heroine, interesting storyline and great writing. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8020535479153280258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2288381082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8702354825403165851"><b>4.5 stars </b><br/><br/>Such an unexpected powerful and moving read. I’m still forcing these foreign lumps in my throat back in as I’m writing this review. I have read countless books on mental illness but I find this book very exceptional because of the constructive and encouraging way the author portrayed a teenage girl with OCD. I appreciate so much the relationship between <b>Sam</b> and her psychiatrist, even involving Sam’s mom in actually contributing with her therapy at home. I love that their talk therapy s</span>
  <span id="freeText8702354825403165851" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars </b><br /><br />Such an unexpected powerful and moving read. I’m still forcing these foreign lumps in my throat back in as I’m writing this review. I have read countless books on mental illness but I find this book very exceptional because of the constructive and encouraging way the author portrayed a teenage girl with OCD. I appreciate so much the relationship between <b>Sam</b> and her psychiatrist, even involving Sam’s mom in actually contributing with her therapy at home. I love that their talk therapy seems genuinely comforting and therapeutic. <br /><br /><i>
  <b> “I’m not making you do anything. Whether or not you tell him is entirely up to you. I’m merely reminding you to embrace who you are and surround yourself with people who do the same.” </b>
</i><br /><br />The story becomes even more interesting when Sam finds a great avenue to refocus her overactive brain and imagination and her anxiety over her relationship with her popular friends through Poetry Corner where she meets these awesome people and adorably, her love interest, <b>AJ.</b> (Love the choice of name). *winks* <br /><br />I was enjoying the story so much at this point but then the turning point suddenly strikes out of nowhere leaving me completely stunned because I so, totally, completely did not see that coming. Goosebumps were everywhere as I started reconciling the earlier events of the story to the shocking revelation near the end. It was heartbreaking and groundbreaking at the same time and I love how <b>Sue</b> the therapist connects the dots to make the most logical explanation as to what Sam was experiencing. <br /><br />I understand that somewhere along the way, the plot became a bit too unrealistic and failed quite a bit to address certain serious issues in the novel, but the important positive messages, wonderful, relatable, witty writing, its unexpected plot twists and surprises and the little beautiful pieces of poetry scattered throughout the novel made up of for the book's few shortcomings. Let me share one of my favorite poems: <br /><br /><b> <i>“These walls heard <br />me when no <br />one else could.<br /><br />They gave my <br />words a home, <br />kept them safe. <br /><br />Cheered, cried, listened<br />Changed my life<br />for the better.<br /><br />It wasn’t enough, <br />But they heard<br />every last word.” </i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8702354825403165851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1156640739" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156640739" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413275441p2/10890208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1156640739?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=omg-the-cover-people">omg-the-cover-people</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=e-arc">e-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=i-cried">i-cried</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=not-bad-at-all">not-bad-at-all</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1156640739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18040270289188310924">See more reviews at <a href='http://yamidnightreads.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>YA Midnight Reads</a><br/><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/><em>Every Last Word </em>is one of those books that had me wanting to smash it into a pulp from page 1, but had me sniffling a bit during the last few chapters.<br/><br/>This story follows Sam, a girl dealing who was diagnosed with Purely Obsessional OCD (aka Pure-O) at the age of 11. While she may look perfectly fine on the outside, each day she is battling with the uncontrollable thoughts that consume her.<br/><br/><strong>I wasn't quite sure I picked up the same book as everyone else</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText18040270289188310924" style="display:none">See more reviews at <a href="http://yamidnightreads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Midnight Reads</a><br /><br /><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br /><em>Every Last Word </em>is one of those books that had me wanting to smash it into a pulp from page 1, but had me sniffling a bit during the last few chapters.<br /><br />This story follows Sam, a girl dealing who was diagnosed with Purely Obsessional OCD (aka Pure-O) at the age of 11. While she may look perfectly fine on the outside, each day she is battling with the uncontrollable thoughts that consume her.<br /><br /><strong>I wasn't quite sure I picked up the same book as everyone else when I was a few chapters into the novel.</strong> Why? Because most of my friends gave this book 4 or 5 stars and there was I, reading along thinking that this was one of the worst books I've ever read on mental illnesses. And the main reason of that was because <strong>I HATE Sam (the main character)'s so called friends.</strong> They're the 'popular' and 'I-think-I'm-prettier-than-all-of-you' girls at school and every girl hates them and every guy loves them. Yeah, that kinda group. Hellooo, high school social hierarchy. Anyway, <strong>Sam's friends pissed me off. Majorly. So much that I was ready to just give up on the book altogether.</strong> Within their little posse, the 'main girl', Alexis (of course that's her name &lt;.&lt;), has basically created her own social ladder amongst the 4 other girls she calls her best friends.<br /><blockquote>"Not Hailey. You." [Alexis] pokes my collarbone. And now I know precisely where I reside on her social ladder: Second rung from the bottom. Hailey occupies the last one, and as soon as she learns I'm invited to Alexis's birthday and she's not, she'll know it too.</blockquote><br /><strong>I actually find it comical how stupidly shallow their friendship is. It's so fake and well, childish. </strong><br /><blockquote>"You have no idea how sad I've been, Samantha. I felt horrible not asking you. Even though our moms weren't friends in preschool, you and I were best friends in kindergarten!"</blockquote><br />In short, Alexis had to choose 2 of her 4 friends to go to the spa with because her mom only got 3 reservations, so Alexis decides to choose the two girls she was best friends with first. <strong>And, since all of them met each other at the same time, Alexis chooses the two girls whose mums were friends with first instead.</strong> WHAT. THE. FUCK. If I only got three reservations to the spa and had more than that many close friends, I'd ditch the spa and go someplace else because friends &gt; going to some fancy pants spa.<br /><br /><strong>Surprisingly enough, this book did a 180 spin soon later and progressively got better. </strong>Sure, Sam still had these hella annoying and fake friends, but I started to get over that because we see less of them the more involved Sam becomes with her new friends. I particularly love Caroline, who is just such a supportive friend and funky girl that wears the best t-shirts. She also suffers from depression, though I personally would have liked to look into that a little more (but I totally get why the author did not). <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[OH MY GAWD I CANONT BELIEVE THAT SHE WASN'T BLOODY REAL. I loved the twist but gah... WHY YOU DO THIS TO MY FEELS? I have trust issues now. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />In terms of the romance, I am really torn about it. AJ is really weary about Sam during the first half of this book because back in 4th grade, she and her 'friends' bullied AJ so bad that he feared his own name and had speech problems. If you know me, you know I love, love, LOVE the hate to love romance trope when executed correctly and well, this one just didn't give me the feels I was told I was gonna get. While I can see how AJ and Sam's relationship works, I just don't ship it hard.<br /><br /><strong>I think <em>Every Last Word </em>is a very important novel to read.</strong> Sure, it's not too promising starting off, but by the end of the book, I can definitely say I knew a lot more about OCD than I started off with. It opened my eyes to see the whole spectrum of OCD - there isn't just one type and there are subcategories. I definitely recommend to <strong>read the acknowledgements</strong> for this book. <strong>I got a little teary just from that, and I love how much effort and dedication Stone took to make this story as genuine as possible.</strong> And she did a pretty damn good job, in the end.<br /><p>
  <em>~Thank you Disney Hyperion for the review copy!~</em>
</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="18040270289188310924" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2143838522" />
    <a title="Maureen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10762033-maureen"><img alt="Maureen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398557569p2/10762033.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2143838522?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maureen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maureen" href="/user/show/10762033-maureen">Maureen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2143838522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16864617363919231777">3.5/5 Stars<br/><br/>This was a really great book! I can’t totally speak for the mental illness representation (and I looked for a few reviews but didn’t find much), but it seemed very respectful and well done to me. It didn’t trivialize the issue, the main character had a very supportive family, and had a great therapist she visited regularly. All of those things are usual seen in a negative light so it was great to see them positively here.<br/>The story was entertaining except for one *spoilery* aspect that</span>
  <span id="freeText16864617363919231777" style="display:none">3.5/5 Stars<br /><br />This was a really great book! I can’t totally speak for the mental illness representation (and I looked for a few reviews but didn’t find much), but it seemed very respectful and well done to me. It didn’t trivialize the issue, the main character had a very supportive family, and had a great therapist she visited regularly. All of those things are usual seen in a negative light so it was great to see them positively here.<br />The story was entertaining except for one *spoilery* aspect that would have been much better with more mystery. I prefer subtext and subtly to being hit over the head with foreshadowing to the point that things are spelled out for you.<br />Overall the story was great and portrayed mental illness well, but was missing subtext and a deeper heart. I would still recommend it, though!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16864617363919231777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
