<div id="review_1011792326" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1011792326" />
    <a title="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source"><img alt="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586156113p2/6511257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1011792326?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" href="/user/show/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source">Sue (Hollywood News Source)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=favorite-otps">favorite-otps</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=diverse-books">diverse-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=alert-the-authorities-i-ship-it">alert-the-authorities-i-ship-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=netgallery-arc">netgallery-arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1011792326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4607233249515720162"><blockquote><br/>These walls heard<br/>me when no<br/>one else could.<br/><br/>They gave my <br/>words a home,<br/>kept them safe.<br/><br/>Cheered, cried, listened.<br/>Changed my life<br/>for the better.<br/><br/>It wasn’t enough.<br/>But they heard<br/>Every last word.<br/></blockquote><br/><br/><b>This is a very surprising book. Look at the glowing reviews because the hype is real. </b><br/><br/>A lot of us frequently use “OCD” figuratively. Nowadays, “OCD” is synonymous to the word perfectionist, a person who likes things in order, or a person who is neat. We throw this word very lightly, but do we honestly know what it</span>
  <span id="freeText4607233249515720162" style="display:none"><blockquote><br />These walls heard<br />me when no<br />one else could.<br /><br />They gave my <br />words a home,<br />kept them safe.<br /><br />Cheered, cried, listened.<br />Changed my life<br />for the better.<br /><br />It wasn’t enough.<br />But they heard<br />Every last word.<br /></blockquote><br /><br /><b>This is a very surprising book. Look at the glowing reviews because the hype is real. </b><br /><br />A lot of us frequently use “OCD” figuratively. Nowadays, “OCD” is synonymous to the word perfectionist, a person who likes things in order, or a person who is neat. We throw this word very lightly, but do we honestly know what it means? This book defined one of the plenty cases of OCD. Not the quirky kind, but the pitch-black type that could make a person question their self and perception of reality.<br /><br />Every Last Word is the story of Samantha McAllister, she is your standard YA contemporary protagonist. She is popular and part of the “elite” group, except for the part, she has emotional baggage hanging on her shoulder. Sam has OCD, one that thrives on dark and obsessional thoughts.<br /><br />Like Sam, her friends are your standard YA contemporary friends. High school cliques could be vicious like a pack of wolves.  They could turn animal in a second. They will either enthusiastically lick someone’s face or tear their whole life apart. There is no middle ground. For this reason, Sam is aware, she needs to expand her social life. Until one day, she meets Caroline.<br /><br />Caroline introduces her to the Poet’s Corner, where she met a group of outcast students bonding over words and music.<br /><br />I am easily attracted to books that revolve around mental health issue. And lately there has been an influx demand of this in Young Adult, which is very marvelous, because we are spreading awareness.<br /><br />Honestly, there is nothing remotely new in <em>Every Last Word.  </em>I have seen and read this type of book. I typically shelf this type of books as my favorite. For instance, a popular group of friends who could turn on you in a second, a promising new bunch of misfit for friends, an outcast guy and a chameleon slash submissive protagonist. What makes this book so distinctive and extraordinary is the authentic portrayal of a teenager grappling with an OCD.<br /><br />Every Last Word explored the nuance of mental illness, and its different varieties. The reality of someone struggling with it, and how it also affects their family and friends. Stone provided the plot with supplementary well researched facts and gut wrenching scenario that will certainly bring misty waters in a reader’s eye.<br /><br /><em>“Really, Sue? Special?”</em><br /><br /><em>“Very. Your brain works differently, Sam. Sometimes it does things that scare you. But it’s very special, and so are you.”</em><br /><br /><em>“Thank you.”</em><br /><br />In addition, this book captures the toxic friendship, a person can’t easily break away from. Because he or she had known them their entire life. There is too much history.<br /><br />Bonus: Wonderful characters and cute romance.<br /><br /><em>“Really. We’re just….different, Sam. In every way that matters.”</em><br /><br /><em>We.</em><br /><br />I love how this novel ended, the hope it imparts to the readers. That is a very beautiful message to convey. I will never stop recommending books similarly to <em>Every Last Word.</em><br /><br />Review also posted at <a href="http://youngadulthollywood.com/books/yah-book-review-every-last-word-by-tamara-ireland-stone/#.VYw0WHrnbqA" rel="nofollow noopener">Young Adult Hollywood.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4607233249515720162" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1483797579" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16209654935465381461">I really enjoyed this book. I don't normally enjoy contemporaries that take place in a high school setting but this felt different. I will admit that The writing style is fairly simplistic and the narrator often over explains things. But the main character is very endearing and I enjoyed her journey immensely. There was just something sweet about this book and I feel like it would be very helpful for teens struggling with mental health. It reinforces the message that everyone is different and th</span>
  <span id="freeText16209654935465381461" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book. I don't normally enjoy contemporaries that take place in a high school setting but this felt different. I will admit that The writing style is fairly simplistic and the narrator often over explains things. But the main character is very endearing and I enjoyed her journey immensely. There was just something sweet about this book and I feel like it would be very helpful for teens struggling with mental health. It reinforces the message that everyone is different and there is no concrete definition of normal - especially when it comes to how your brain works. </span>

<div id="review_1237507601" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1237507601" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1237507601?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1237507601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15134073019640376252"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com'>www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com</a><br/><br/>I thought this was a damn good book. The ending really took me by surprise, I never saw that one coming, although I knew something seemed a bit weird. <br/><br/>Samantha has OCD since she was a child and is on medication for anxiety. Sam has hidden this fact from her so called friends all of her life. These girls that she grew up with were mean and she was always afraid to pull away from them. <br/><br/>Then one day she meets a really nice girl named Caroline. She takes Sam into </span>
  <span id="freeText15134073019640376252" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com">www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com</a><br><br>I thought this was a damn good book. The ending really took me by surprise, I never saw that one coming, although I knew something seemed a bit weird. <br><br>Samantha has OCD since she was a child and is on medication for anxiety. Sam has hidden this fact from her so called friends all of her life. These girls that she grew up with were mean and she was always afraid to pull away from them. <br><br>Then one day she meets a really nice girl named Caroline. She takes Sam into a different world where the so called "misfits" of the school hang out. They are down in the basement of the school and have the coolest room set up in there. They tell poetry and just have really good times together. The walls of the room are covered in poetry where you glue it up when you are done reading it. <br><br>Sam meets a boy named Aj through this group, he doesn't want her there when she first shows up. It turns out she did some horrible things to Aj when he was young along with her jerk friends. But, she writes a beautiful poem telling about her sorrow for the things she did and how ashamed she feels for being that person. Aj starts to come around and they form a beautiful friendship. <br><br>Meeting these new people is helping Sam with her OCD, she feels more calm. This doesn't heal her, but it helps her cope. When your around relaxed, nice people you tend to feel that way yourself. And Sam is starting to pull away from the group she is in... yay! <br><br>Aj and Sam begin a slow romance together that blooms in about the middle of the book. I think it was wonderful how they bonded and felt serene around each other. Sam has to decide if she's going to share her secret with Sam. Will he leave her because of her OCD? What do you think? I think you should read the book :) <br><br>Kudos to the author for mentioning some things about OCD at the end of the book. It's hard for people to understand anyone with different kinds of mental disorders. And if you don't understand it, don't make fun of it, don't think they are weird, don't think you are better, in fact... keep your trap shut unless you have something nice to say! <br><br>Fin <br><br><a href="http://s1379.photobucket.com/user/melmartD11/media/book%20banner_zpsh916lrql.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437402575i/15581842._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo book banner_zpsh916lrql.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dXlkPOzYMftPLmDAMthcjmDIqhp92/fcQa0vth8TJDo0frYDxxJ7MgVyrpcB+uEdy0yLp3qIjaxY8cSKh82eAA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1RazRHbuwKMB4uhj0NQ5PEVyEuSlB4SGvRdeGmZo5gSUEWF7XSSKaku+JjTj9oSv7vYzWaJU/vakS7Um/rZcPg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1699926534163001679">TAMARA IRELAND STONE spent nearly two decades in the technology industry before she began writing middle grade and young adult fiction. She feels lucky to say she's had two careers she's loved.<br/><br/>Her New York Times bestseller, EVERY LAST WORD, won the Cybils Young Adult Fiction Award, the Georgia Peach Book Award, and was a YALSA Teens' Top Ten pick; LITTLE DO WE KNOW won the NCIBA Golden Poppy Award</span>
  <span id="freeText1699926534163001679" style="display:none">TAMARA IRELAND STONE spent nearly two decades in the technology industry before she began writing middle grade and young adult fiction. She feels lucky to say she's had two careers she's loved.<br /><br />Her New York Times bestseller, EVERY LAST WORD, won the Cybils Young Adult Fiction Award, the Georgia Peach Book Award, and was a YALSA Teens' Top Ten pick; LITTLE DO WE KNOW won the NCIBA Golden Poppy Award for Young Adult Fiction; and her debut novel, TIME BETWEEN US, has been published in over twenty languages. The first book in her middle-grade series, CLICK'D, was a Sunshine State Young Readers Award pick, a Kids' Indie Next pick, a Cybils Award Nominee, and an NCIBA Golden Poppy nominee. <br /><br />Tamara is a proud nerd, vinyl collector, and movie lover. She burns everything she cooks. <br /><br />She lives in the San Francisco Bay Area.</span>
